## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt with features t and P is a classic population-dynamics setup where the growth rate depends on current population size (density dependence) and possibly explicit time forcing (seasonality, trends, interventions). Typical models are first-order ordinary differential equations for P(t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, constant per-capita rate)
- Exponential with immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (constant net inflow/outflow)
- Density-dependent (quadratic) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (simple crowding/competition approximation)
- θ-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (flexible strength/shape of crowding)
- Gompertz growth (log-density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with multiplicative regulation)
- Richards (generalized logistic family): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (tunable sigmoid shape; includes special cases)
- Allee effect (strong Allee): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P, saturation at high P)
- Allee effect (smooth/weak form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (P / (P + c2)) (reduced growth at low P without sharp threshold)
- Harvesting (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed extraction effort, can cause collapse)
- Harvesting (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (mortality/harvest proportional to abundance)
- Saturating harvest (Holling type II in P): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (limited harvesting capacity at high P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (effective capacity drifting over time)
- Pulse/step intervention (time threshold): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * Max(t - c3, 0) * P (time-triggered added mortality or control)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth analysis: structures of the form dP_dt = P * g(P, t) encode that births/deaths scale with abundance; g decreasing in P indicates competition.
- Crowding/competition: negative P**2 (or higher powers) terms represent increasing per-capita mortality or reduced fecundity with density.
- Carrying-capacity behavior: factors like (1 - c * P) or (1 - c * P**θ) imply an equilibrium near P ≈ (1 / c)**(1/θ) where growth changes sign.
- Gompertz-type regulation: log(c / P) implies regulation depends on log-density; yields asymmetric sigmoids with slow approach to the ceiling.
- Allee effect signature: inclusion of (P - c) or a low-P attenuation factor P/(P + c) creates reduced/negative growth at small populations (critical thresholds possible).
- Harvesting/mortality separation: subtractive terms (e.g., -c, -c*P, -c*P/(P+c)) indicate external removal; constant vs proportional vs saturating harvest produce distinct low-P outcomes.
- Seasonality/forcing: sinusoidal dependence on t in the multiplicative rate (c0 + c1*sin(...)) indicates periodic environment; can generate oscillatory P(t) even in 1D ODEs.
- Nonstationary environment: explicit t trends (e.g., exp(c*t), polynomial in t) in growth or regulation terms represent changing resources/climate/management over time.
- Regime-change interventions: Max(t-c,0) or other time-threshold terms indicate policy/onset effects that switch dynamics after a specific time.

Structure desc      : Additive P-only model with linear term, fractional power P^{0.674} scaled, a constant, a tanh, and two decaying exponentials in P. The tanh term is negligible because c4≈-0.0229 is very small and tanh(-0.2249P) is bounded; the two exponentials have similar rates (c7≈-0.0255, c9≈-0.0294) and nearly opposite amplitudes (c6≈-29.74, c8≈+30.14), causing strong cancellation near P=0 and leaving a small residual shape. Thus the behavior is dominated by 0.1268P + 0.1282*P^{0.674} plus a small correction from the “difference of exponentials.” Approximate simplification: ≈ 0.1268P + 0.1282P^{0.674} + (30.14e^{-0.0294P} - 29.74e^{-0.0255P}) - 0.419.

GT: c0*(c1 - exp(-c2*P))*P + c3*P*exp(-c4*t)

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: 0.11782*(1 - exp(-0.02723*P))*P + 0.11782*P*exp(-0.02723*t)**

Expanding: **GT = 0.11782*P - 0.11782*P*exp(-0.02723*P) + 0.11782*P*exp(-0.02723*t)**

The GT has three terms:
1. A linear term in P: `a*P`
2. A term `b*P*exp(-c*P)` (product of P and exponential in P)
3. A term `d*P*exp(-e*t)` (product of P and exponential in t)

Key basis functions needed: `P`, `P*exp(negative*P)`, `P*exp(negative*t)`.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of these basis functions.

**Critical observations:**
- The GT requires a `P*exp(c*t)` term (with c < 0). Candidates without any `exp(t)` term or `t`-dependent term that can produce `P*exp(-ct)` cannot match.
- The GT requires `P*exp(c*P)` (with c < 0). This is distinct from `exp(c*P)` alone.
- Terms like `tanh`, `sin`, `log`, `P^c`, `1/(P+c)`, `sqrt(P)`, `t/sqrt(P+c)`, `t*(P+c)^(1/3)` are all linearly independent from the GT's basis functions and must have zero coefficients.

Let me systematically go through candidates, focusing on whether they can produce both `P*exp(c*P)` AND `P*exp(c*t)`.

**Candidates with exp(c*t) term:**
4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 22, 23, 27, 35, 36, 41, 45, 46, 47, 48

Among these, I need `P*exp(c*P)` — but most candidates have `exp(c*P)` without the P multiplier. Let me check which ones can produce `P*exp(c*P)`.

**Candidate 5:** `P*c0/(P*c1+c2) + P^c3*c4 + c5*exp(P*c6) + c7*exp(c8*t) + c9/(P*c1+c2)`

This has `exp(P*c6)` (not P*exp), `exp(c8*t)` (not P*exp). Can't produce `P*exp(-cP)` or `P*exp(-ct)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 7:** Same structure as 5 with constant instead of 1/(...). Same issue. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 48:** `P*c0*log(P*c1+1)/(P+c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t)/(P+c2) + P*c5/(P+c2) + P/(P+c2) + c6/(P+c2) + c7*log(P*c1+1)/(P+c2) + c8*exp(c4*t)/(P+c2)`

This has `P*exp(c4*t)/(P+c2)`. If c2=0, this becomes `c3*exp(c4*t)`, not `P*exp(c4*t)`. The log terms can't produce `P*exp(cP)`. **NO MATCH**

Going through all candidates systematically: None of them have both `P*exp(c*P)` and `P*exp(c*t)` as available basis functions. Every candidate either:
- Lacks `exp(c*t)` entirely, or
- Has `exp(c*P)` without the P multiplier (can't produce `P*exp(cP)`), or
- Has `exp(c*t)` without the P multiplier (can't produce `P*exp(ct)`).

Since `P*exp(cP)` cannot be decomposed into sums of `exp(cP)`, `P`, `P^a`, `log(...)`, `tanh(...)`, etc. (these are linearly independent), none of the candidates can match the GT.
